## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide

## Objective

Analyze the changes between Terraform v1.9.0 and v1.10.0 and produce a comprehensive migration guide for users upgrading from v1.9.0 to v1.10.0.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Terraform codebase:
- **v1.9.0**: implemented in `/workspace/terraform-v1.9.0/` (commit 7637a92)
- **v1.10.0**: implemented in `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/` (commit 24236f4)

Your task is to identify breaking changes and behavioral changes that affect users, then document migration steps.

## Required Analysis

Your migration guide must cover:

1. **S3 Backend Changes**
   - Removal of deprecated IAM role assumption attributes
   - Migration to `assume_role` block syntax
   - New S3 native state locking support

2. **Moved Blocks Syntax Changes**
   - New requirement to prepend `resource.` identifier when referencing resources with type names matching top-level blocks/keywords
   - Impact on existing `moved` blocks in configurations

3. **Sensitive Value Handling**
   - Changes to mark propagation in conditional expressions
   - When sensitive marks are now preserved (previously lost)
   - How to use `nonsensitive()` to override when needed

4. **Ephemeral Resources and Values** (new feature with migration implications)
   - Introduction of ephemeral input variables and outputs
   - New ephemeral resource mode
   - Impact on secret handling in state files

## Expected Output

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` with the following structure:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the upgrade and major themes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Each breaking change with:
   - What changed and why
   - Before/after code examples
   - Step-by-step migration instructions
   - Common pitfalls to avoid
3. **New Features with Migration Impact** - Features that change how users should write Terraform
4. **Testing Your Migration** - How to validate the upgrade was successful
5. **Rollback Guidance** - How to safely rollback if needed

## Evaluation

Your review will be evaluated on detection accuracy and fix quality.

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changes in specific files
- Look for UPGRADE notes in release documentation
- Examine test files to understand behavioral changes
- Check for deprecation warnings and removed features
- Pay attention to changes in internal/backend/remote-state/s3/, internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract.go, and lang/marks/ directories

Good luck!

# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide

## Overview

Terraform v1.10.0 (released November 27, 2024) is a minor release in the stable v1.0 series that introduces new features and fixes for issues in v1.9.0. This guide covers the breaking changes and behavioral updates that may require changes to your Terraform configurations.

### Major Themes
- **S3 Backend Improvements**: Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and support for S3 native state locking
- **Moved Block Enhancements**: Better handling of resource type names that match reserved keywords
- **Sensitive Value Handling**: Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions
- **New Ephemeral Feature**: Support for ephemeral variables, outputs, and resources that aren't persisted to state

## Breaking Changes

### 1. S3 Backend: IAM Role Assumption Attribute Removal

#### What Changed
Terraform v1.10 removes deprecated root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes have been replaced with a structured `assume_role` block that provides better organization and clarity.

The following attributes have been **removed and are no longer supported**:
- `role_arn`
- `session_name`
- `external_id`
- `assume_role_duration_seconds`
- `assume_role_policy`
- `assume_role_policy_arns`
- `assume_role_tags`
- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`

#### Before (v1.9.0)
```hcl
terraform {
  backend "s3" {
    bucket     = "my-terraform-state"
    key        = "prod/terraform.tfstate"
    region     = "us-east-1"

    # Deprecated attributes - will NOT work in v1.10
    role_arn                       = "arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role"
    session_name                   = "terraform-session"
    external_id                    = "my-ext
... (truncated)

## 📋 Documentation Summary

The migration guide (`/workspace/documentation.md`) includes:

### **1. Breaking Changes** (3 major areas)

- **S3 Backend IAM Role Removal**: Detailed migration from deprecated root-level attributes to the new `assume_role` block structure with:
  - Complete mapping table of old attributes to new ones
  - Before/after code examples
  - Step-by-step migration instructions
  - Common pitfalls

- **Moved Block Reserved Keywords**: Guide for handling resource type names that match reserved keywords (`count`, `each`, `local`, `module`, `path`, `self`, `terraform`, `var`, `template`, `lazy`, `arg`)
  - Clear examples of when to use `resource.` prefix
  - Syntax fixes and verification methods

- **Sensitive Value Mark Propagation**: Explanation of improved mark handling in conditional expressions
  - How v1.10 preserves sensitive marks better than v1.9
  - Using `nonsensitive()` function to override marks
  - Impact on output declarations

### **2. New Features with Migration Impact**

- **Ephemeral Resources and Values**: Introduction to the public beta ephemeral feature
  - Ephemeral input variables and outputs
  - The `ephemeralasnull()` function
  - Valid contexts for ephemeral values
  
- **S3 Native State Locking**: Information on the new `use_lockfile` parameter and IAM policy updates

### **3. Practical Sections**

- **Testing Guide**: Pre-migration, during migration, and specific test cases
- **Rollback Guidance**: Step-by-step instructions for reverting to v1.9 if needed
- **Common Issues**: Troubleshooting with solutions
- **Upgrade Checklist**: Complete list of items to verify

Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated.   "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: ## 1.10.0 (November 27, 2024)\n2: \n3: NEW FEATURES:\n4:  - **Ephemeral resources**: Ephemeral resources are read anew during each phase of Terraform evaluation, and cannot be persisted to state storage. Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\n7: \n8: BUG FIXES:\n9: \n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\n24: \n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\n26: \n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\n32: \n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\n34: \n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. 27. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 (released November 27, 2024) is a minor release in the stable v1.0 series that introduces new features and fixes for issues in v1.9.0. This guide covers the breaking changes and behavioral updates that may require changes to your Terraform configurations.\n\n### Major Themes\n- **S3 Backend Improvements**: Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and support for S3 native state locking\n- **Moved Block Enhancements**: Better handling of resource type names that match reserved keywords\n- **Sensitive Value Handling**: Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions\n- **New Ephemeral Feature**: Support for ephemeral variables, outputs, and resources that aren't persisted to state\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: IAM Role Assumption Attribute Removal\n\n#### What Changed\nTerraform v1.10 removes deprecated root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes have been replaced with a structured `assume_role` block that provides better organization and clarity.\n\nThe following attributes have been **removed and are no longer supported**:\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket     = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key        = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region     = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Deprecated attributes - will NOT work in v1.10\n    role_arn                       = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n    session_name                   = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                    = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds   = 3600\n    assume_role_policy             = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags               = { Environment = \"prod\" }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # New block syntax - required in v1.10\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn           = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      session_name       = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id        = \"my-external-id\"\n      duration           = 3600\n      policy             = jsonencode({...})\n      tags               = { Environment = \"prod\" }\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n1. **Identify all S3 backend configurations** in your Terraform code that use deprecated root-level IAM role attributes\n2. **Create an `assume_role` block** within your S3 backend configuration\n3. **Migrate each attribute** according to the mapping table below:\n\n| Removed Attribute | New Location |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arn` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n4. **If you use variables** to set these values, you can continue using the same variable references within the new block:\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = var.bucket_name\n    key    = var.key_name\n    region = var.aws_region\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn     = var.role_arn\n      session_name = var.session_name\n      external_id  = var.external_id\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n5. **Test your configuration** by running `terraform init` to reinitialize the backend\n6. **Verify the upgrade** by running `terraform plan` to ensure state is properly accessible\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n- \u274c Forgetting to move ALL old attributes to the new block structure\n- \u274c Attempting to use both old and new style attributes (only new style works)\n- \u274c Not updating variable references if you were using variables to set these values\n- \u274c Assuming the old attributes will be silently ignored (they will cause configuration validation errors)\n\n#### Rollback Strategy\nIf you need to rollback to v1.9.0 after upgrading:\n1. Convert your `assume_role` block back to root-level attributes\n2. Reinitialize the backend with `terraform init`\n3. Verify that state is still accessible\n\n---\n\n### 2. Moved Block Syntax: Reserved Keyword Handling\n\n#### What Changed\nTerraform v1.10 now enforces stricter parsing of `moved` block resource addresses. Resource type names that match reserved keywords (such as `local`, `each`, `self`, etc.) are no longer valid without explicit qualification. You must now prepend `resource.` to the address when targeting such resources.\n\n#### Reserved Keywords\nThe following keywords are now reserved and cannot be used as resource type names in `moved` blocks without the `resource.` prefix:\n- `count`, `each`, `local`, `module`, `path`, `self`, `terraform`, `var`, `template`, `lazy`, `arg`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource named \"local\" (the type), this worked in v1.9\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = local.renamed_example\n}\n\n# If you had a data source named \"var\", this worked in v1.9\nmoved {\n  from = data.var.example\n  to   = data.var.renamed_example\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n```hcl\n# In v1.10, you must prepend \"resource.\" when the type name matches a reserved keyword\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = resource.local.renamed_example\n}\n\n# Same applies to data sources\nmoved {\n  from = data.var.example\n  to   = data.var.renamed_example\n}\n\n# Regular resource types (not matching reserved keywords) work as before\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.example\n  to   = aws_instance.renamed_example\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n1. **Run `terraform validate`** to identify any `moved` blocks that use reserved keyword resource type names\n2. **Review the error messages** - Terraform will tell you which references are using reserved keywords\n3. **Update `moved` blocks** by adding `resource.` prefix to addresses that match reserved keywords\n4. **Focus on these patterns**:\n   - If your resource type name is one of the reserved words, prepend `resource.`\n   - You only need to update the resource type part of the address\n   - Module and resource names themselves don't need changes\n5. **Run `terraform validate`** again to confirm the changes are correct\n\n#### Example Fixes\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (v1.9.0) - causes error in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.config\n  to   = local.app_config\n}\n\n# AFTER (v1.10.0) - now valid\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config\n  to   = resource.local.app_config\n}\n```\n\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (v1.9.0) - causes error in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = var.settings\n  to   = var.application_settings\n}\n\n# AFTER (v1.10.0) - now valid\nmoved {\n  from = data.var.settings\n  to   = data.var.application_settings\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n- \u274c Only updating the `from` address but forgetting to update the `to` address\n- \u274c Adding `resource.` to regular resource types that don't conflict with keywords\n- \u274c Misunderstanding that this only applies to the resource TYPE, not the resource NAME\n- \u274c Not running `terraform validate` to catch these issues early\n\n#### Verification\nRun `terraform validate` to ensure all `moved` blocks are correctly specified:\n```bash\nterraform validate\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. Sensitive Value Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\nTerraform v1.10 improves how sensitive marks are propagated through conditional expressions and `for` expressions. Marks are now combined from all values within the expression to ensure consistency in results and avoid losing sensitive information.\n\n**Key behavior change**: In v1.9, sensitive marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional expressions and unknown values. In v1.10, marks are preserved more accurately.\n\n#### Impact\n- **Improved accuracy**: Your configuration validation may now correctly identify more sensitive values\n- **Potential visibility changes**: You may see outputs marked as sensitive where they weren't in v1.9\n- **Breaking for some workflows**: If you relied on conditional expressions that \"hid\" sensitive marks, you'll see different behavior\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"include_password\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\n# In v1.9, this could lose the sensitive mark in certain conditions\nlocals {\n  config = var.include_password ? {\n    password = var.database_password\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  } : {\n    password = null\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  }\n}\n\n# Output could incorrectly show as non-sensitive\noutput \"config\" {\n  value     = local.config\n  sensitive = false  # This contradicts the actual sensitivity\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"include_password\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\n# In v1.10, the sensitive mark is properly preserved through the conditional\nlocals {\n  config = var.include_password ? {\n    password = var.database_password\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  } : {\n    password = null\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  }\n}\n\n# Output must now declare it as sensitive OR use nonsensitive() to explicitly remove marks\noutput \"config\" {\n  value = var.include_password ? local.config : {\n    password = null\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  }\n  sensitive = var.include_password  # Now correctly marks as sensitive when needed\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n1. **Run `terraform plan`** and check for warnings about sensitive values in outputs\n2. **Review outputs** that should have marked sensitive data:\n   - Add `sensitive = true` to the output declaration if the output may contain sensitive data\n   - OR use `nonsensitive()` function if you explicitly want to expose non-sensitive parts\n3. **Use the `nonsensitive()` function** to selectively remove sensitive marks:\n```hcl\n# This removes the sensitive mark while preserving non-sensitive parts\noutput \"non_sensitive_config\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(local.config.user)\n}\n```\n\n4. **For complex expressions**, ensure sensitive marks are handled explicitly:\n```hcl\n# When mixing sensitive and non-sensitive in conditionals\nlocals {\n  # Result will be sensitive if any branch uses sensitive data\n  value = var.use_secret ? var.secret_value : \"default_public_value\"\n}\n```\n\n5. **Run `terraform plan` again** to verify mark handling is correct\n\n#### Using `nonsensitive()` to Override Marks\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# You can remove the sensitive mark explicitly if needed\nlocals {\n  config = {\n    key = nonsensitive(var.api_key)  # Explicitly strip sensitive mark\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n- \u274c Not updating output blocks that now show warnings about missing `sensitive` declaration\n- \u274c Using `nonsensitive()` to hide sensitive values (they're still sensitive in state)\n- \u274c Assuming marks automatically propagate without declaring `sensitive = true` on outputs\n- \u274c Mixing sensitive and non-sensitive values without explicitly handling the result\n\n#### When Sensitive Marks Are Preserved\nMarks are combined from ALL values in a conditional expression:\n```hcl\n# Result is always sensitive (combines both branches)\nresult = condition ? sensitive_value : non_sensitive_value\n\n# Both branches have sensitive marks, so result is sensitive\nresult = condition ? sensitive_value_1 : sensitive_value_2\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\n#### What's New\nTerraform v1.10 introduces **ephemeral** data handling, which is available in public beta. Ephemeral values are available during Terraform operations but are NOT written to state files, plan files, or persisted between phases.\n\nThis is useful for managing temporary data like:\n- Authentication tokens with short expiration times\n- Temporary credentials generated during a Terraform run\n- Build artifacts that should not be stored\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n```hcl\n# Define an ephemeral input variable\nvariable \"temporary_auth_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"A short-lived authentication token that won't be stored in state\"\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # This local becomes implicitly ephemeral because it references an ephemeral variable\n  api_config = {\n    token = var.temporary_auth_token\n    endpoint = \"https://api.example.com\"\n  }\n}\n\nresource \"example_resource\" \"config\" {\n  # You can only use ephemeral values in specific contexts\n  token = var.temporary_auth_token\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs (Child Modules Only)\n```hcl\n# In a child module, you can create ephemeral outputs\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value     = var.temp_token\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary credentials not written to state\"\n}\n\n# This output can be referenced by parent modules but won't be persisted\n```\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull()` Function\nUse `ephemeralasnull()` to replace ephemeral values with `null` when you need non-ephemeral output:\n```hcl\nvariable \"secret_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Create a local that contains some ephemeral data\nlocals {\n  config = {\n    token = var.secret_token\n    name  = \"my-service\"\n  }\n}\n\n# Output the config with ephemeral values converted to null\noutput \"config\" {\n  value = ephemeralasnull(local.config)\n  description = \"Config with non-ephemeral values only\"\n  # Result: { token = null, name = \"my-service\" }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n- Ephemeral values are in **public beta** and workflows may change\n- Ephemeral outputs are **only allowed in child modules**, not root modules\n- Ephemeral values can only be referenced in specific contexts:\n  - Other ephemeral variables\n  - Local values\n  - Ephemeral resources\n  - Ephemeral outputs\n- If you need to output ephemeral data, use `ephemeralasnull()` to make it non-ephemeral\n\n#### Using Ephemeral Values for Secrets\n```hcl\n# Replace sensitive + ephemeral workflow\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true  # NOT stored in state at all\n  # sensitive = true  # No longer needed when using ephemeral\n}\n\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"main\" {\n  password = var.db_password\n  # Password is temporary, exists only during the operation\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### S3 Backend: Native State Locking (Experimental)\n\n#### What's New\nThe S3 backend now supports optional S3 native state locking as an experimental feature. This allows you to use S3 Object Lock for state management without requiring DynamoDB.\n\n#### How It Works\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Enable S3 native locking (experimental)\n    use_lockfile   = true\n\n    # Can still use DynamoDB alongside S3 locking\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Lock File Naming\nWhen `use_lockfile = true`:\n- Lock file is placed in the same location as the state file\n- Named identically to the state file with `.tflock` extension\n- Example: if state is `prod/terraform.tfstate`, lock is `prod/terraform.tfstate.tflock`\n\n#### Important: IAM and Bucket Policies\n**You must update your S3 bucket policies and IAM policies** to include permissions for the lock file:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Principal\": {\n        \"AWS\": \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      },\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:GetObject\",\n        \"s3:PutObject\",\n        \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": [\n        \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/*\",\n        \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/*.tflock\"  # Add this line\n      ]\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\n1. **Update IAM permissions** to allow access to `.tflock` files\n2. **Enable `use_lockfile`** in your S3 backend configuration\n3. **DynamoDB locking** is still supported and will be used alongside S3 locking\n4. **Future versions** will deprecate DynamoDB-based locking\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Testing\n```bash\n# 1. Validate your current configuration with v1.9\nterraform validate\n\n# 2. Create a test plan\nterraform plan -out=test.tfplan\n\n# 3. Verify the plan makes sense\nterraform show test.tfplan\n```\n\n### Migration Testing\n```bash\n# 1. Upgrade Terraform\nterraform version  # Should show v1.10.0 or later\n\n# 2. Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# 3. Check for any issues\n# This should report any deprecated attribute usage\nterraform plan\n\n# 4. If using S3 backend with IAM role attributes:\n# - Update to assume_role block\n# - Run: terraform init\n# - Verify: terraform plan\n\n# 5. If using moved blocks with reserved keywords:\n# - Check validate output for errors\n# - Update address syntax\n# - Run: terraform validate\n```\n\n### Specific Test Cases\n\n#### Test S3 Backend Changes\n```bash\n# After updating assume_role block\ncd your-terraform-config/\nterraform init\n\n# Verify state is accessible\nterraform state list\n\n# Try a plan operation\nterraform plan\n```\n\n#### Test Moved Block Changes\n```bash\n# Run validation to catch syntax errors\nterraform validate\n\n# If there are moved blocks, check plan\nterraform plan\n# Should show successful moves, not errors\n```\n\n#### Test Sensitive Mark Changes\n```bash\n# Plan should show outputs with correct sensitive marking\nterraform plan\n\n# Check if any outputs should have sensitive = true\nterraform plan -json | grep -A5 \"sensitive\"\n```\n\n#### Test Ephemeral Values (if used)\n```bash\n# Ephemeral variables should work in plan\nterraform plan -var 'temp_token=short-lived-value'\n\n# Value should not appear in state\nterraform state show <resource>\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Rolling Back from v1.10 to v1.9\n\nIf you need to rollback to v1.9:\n\n#### S3 Backend Rollback\n```bash\n# 1. Convert assume_role block back to root-level attributes\n# OLD (v1.10) - in terraform { backend \"s3\" { } }\n# assume_role {\n#   role_arn           = \"arn:...\"\n#   session_name       = \"session\"\n#   external_id        = \"id\"\n# }\n\n# NEW (v1.9) - in terraform { backend \"s3\" { } }\n# role_arn                       = \"arn:...\"\n# session_name                   = \"session\"\n# external_id                    = \"id\"\n\n# 2. Reinitialize backend\nterraform init\n\n# 3. Verify state is accessible\nterraform plan\n```\n\n#### Moved Block Rollback\n```bash\n# 1. Remove \"resource.\" prefixes from moved block addresses\n# OLD (v1.10)\n# moved {\n#   from = resource.local.example\n#   to   = resource.local.renamed\n# }\n\n# NEW (v1.9)\n# moved {\n#   from = local.example\n#   to   = local.renamed\n# }\n\n# 2. Validate\nterraform validate\n```\n\n#### Downgrade Process\n```bash\n# 1. Make configuration changes as noted above\n# 2. Uninstall v1.10\nterraform version\n\n# 3. Install v1.9\n# Use your package manager or download from releases.hashicorp.com\n\n# 4. Verify\nterraform version  # Should show v1.9.x\n\n# 5. Test\nterraform validate\nterraform plan\n```\n\n### Safe Rollback Checklist\n- [ ] Configuration changes reverted\n- [ ] Terraform binary downgraded to v1.9\n- [ ] `terraform init` completed successfully\n- [ ] `terraform validate` passes\n- [ ] `terraform plan` completes without errors\n- [ ] Team members notified of rollback\n\n---\n\n## Common Issues and Solutions\n\n### Issue: \"keyword X is reserved and cannot be used\"\n**Cause**: Using a resource type name that matches a reserved keyword without the `resource.` prefix\n```hcl\n# \u274c Wrong\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = local.renamed\n}\n\n# \u2705 Correct\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = resource.local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n### Issue: S3 Backend refuses deprecated attributes\n**Cause**: Using old root-level IAM attributes instead of `assume_role` block\n```hcl\n# \u274c Won't work in v1.10\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    role_arn     = \"arn:...\"\n    session_name = \"session\"\n  }\n}\n\n# \u2705 Correct way\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn     = \"arn:...\"\n      session_name = \"session\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Issue: Output marked as sensitive unexpectedly\n**Cause**: v1.10 now correctly preserves sensitive marks through conditionals\n```hcl\n# Add sensitive = true to outputs that contain potentially sensitive data\noutput \"config\" {\n  value     = local.config\n  sensitive = var.include_password  # Set based on content\n}\n\n# OR use nonsensitive() to explicitly remove marks\noutput \"public_config\" {\n  value = {\n    user = nonsensitive(local.config.user)\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Issue: \"Ephemeral value not allowed here\"\n**Cause**: Trying to use ephemeral value in a non-ephemeral context\n```hcl\n# \u274c Wrong - using ephemeral variable in a regular resource\nvariable \"token\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\noutput \"token\" {\n  value = var.token  # Error: can't persist ephemeral to state\n}\n\n# \u2705 Correct ways:\noutput \"token\" {\n  value     = var.token\n  ephemeral = true  # Mark output as ephemeral (child modules only)\n}\n\n# OR in root module, convert to non-ephemeral:\noutput \"config\" {\n  value = {\n    user = \"admin\"\n    # token omitted - not using ephemeral value\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Terraform v1.10 Release Notes](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [S3 Backend Configuration Reference](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Moved Block Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/moved)\n- [Ephemeral Variables Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables#exclude-values-from-state)\n- [Sensitive Data in State](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/state/sensitive-data)\n- [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\n\n---\n\n## Support and Questions\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Check the error message carefully** - Terraform usually provides clear guidance on what needs to change\n2. **Run `terraform validate`** to catch syntax and configuration errors\n3. **Review the CHANGELOG** for detailed information on specific changes\n4. **Test in a non-production environment** first\n5. **Post in the [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)** if you encounter unexpected behavior\n\n---\n\n## Upgrade Summary Checklist\n\n- [ ] Review all S3 backend configurations for deprecated IAM attributes\n- [ ] Update S3 backend configurations to use `assume_role` block\n- [ ] Update IAM/bucket policies to allow lock file access (if using `use_lockfile`)\n- [ ] Review all `moved` blocks for reserved keyword resource type names\n- [ ] Update `moved` block syntax to use `resource.` prefix where needed\n- [ ] Run `terraform validate` on all configurations\n- [ ] Test `terraform plan` in a safe environment\n- [ ] Review output blocks for missing `sensitive` declarations\n- [ ] Test with `terraform apply` on a non-critical resource if possible\n- [ ] Document any configuration changes for your team\n- [ ] Update team documentation and runbooks\n\n",

{
  "content": "# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 (released November 27, 2024) is a minor release in the stable v1.0 series that introduces new features and fixes for issues in v1.9.0. This guide covers the breaking changes and behavioral updates that may require changes to your Terraform configurations.\n\n### Major Themes\n- **S3 Backend Improvements**: Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and support for S3 native state locking\n- **Moved Block Enhancements**: Better handling of resource type names that match reserved keywords\n- **Sensitive Value Handling**: Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions\n- **New Ephemeral Feature**: Support for ephemeral variables, outputs, and resources that aren't persisted to state\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: IAM Role Assumption Attribute Removal\n\n#### What Changed\nTerraform v1.10 removes deprecated root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes have been replaced with a structured `assume_role` block that provides better organization and clarity.\n\nThe following attributes have been **removed and are no longer supported**:\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket     = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key        = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region     = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Deprecated attributes - will NOT work in v1.10\n    role_arn                       = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n    session_name                   = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                    = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds   = 3600\n    assume_role_policy             = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags               = { Environment = \"prod\" }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # New block syntax - required in v1.10\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn           = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      session_name       = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id        = \"my-external-id\"\n      duration           = 3600\n      policy             = jsonencode({...})\n      tags               = { Environment = \"prod\" }\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n1. **Identify all S3 backend configurations** in your Terraform code that use deprecated root-level IAM role attributes\n2. **Create an `assume_role` block** within your S3 backend configuration\n3. **Migrate each attribute** according to the mapping table below:\n\n| Removed Attribute | New Location |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arn` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n4. **If you use variables** to set these values, you can continue using the same variable references within the new block:\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = var.bucket_name\n    key    = var.key_name\n    region = var.aws_region\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn     = var.role_arn\n      session_name = var.session_name\n      external_id  = var.external_id\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n5. **Test your configuration** by running `terraform init` to reinitialize the backend\n6. **Verify the upgrade** by running `terraform plan` to ensure state is properly accessible\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n- \u274c Forgetting to move ALL old attributes to the new block structure\n- \u274c Attempting to use both old and new style attributes (only new style works)\n- \u274c Not updating variable references if you were using variables to set these values\n- \u274c Assuming the old attributes will be silently ignored (they will cause configuration validation errors)\n\n#### Rollback Strategy\nIf you need to rollback to v1.9.0 after upgrading:\n1. Convert your `assume_role` block back to root-level attributes\n2. Reinitialize the backend with `terraform init`\n3. Verify that state is still accessible\n\n---\n\n### 2. Moved Block Syntax: Reserved Keyword Handling\n\n#### What Changed\nTerraform v1.10 now enforces stricter parsing of `moved` block resource addresses. Resource type names that match reserved keywords (such as `local`, `each`, `self`, etc.) are no longer valid without explicit qualification. You must now prepend `resource.` to the address when targeting such resources.\n\n#### Reserved Keywords\nThe following keywords are now reserved and cannot be used as resource type names in `moved` blocks without the `resource.` prefix:\n- `count`, `each`, `local`, `module`, `path`, `self`, `terraform`, `var`, `template`, `lazy`, `arg`\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource named \"local\" (the type), this worked in v1.9\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = local.renamed_example\n}\n\n# If you had a data source named \"var\", this worked in v1.9\nmoved {\n  from = data.var.example\n  to   = data.var.renamed_example\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n```hcl\n# In v1.10, you must prepend \"resource.\" when the type name matches a reserved keyword\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = resource.local.renamed_example\n}\n\n# Same applies to data sources\nmoved {\n  from = data.var.example\n  to   = data.var.renamed_example\n}\n\n# Regular resource types (not matching reserved keywords) work as before\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.example\n  to   = aws_instance.renamed_example\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n1. **Run `terraform validate`** to identify any `moved` blocks that use reserved keyword resource type names\n2. **Review the error messages** - Terraform will tell you which references are using reserved keywords\n3. **Update `moved` blocks** by adding `resource.` prefix to addresses that match reserved keywords\n4. **Focus on these patterns**:\n   - If your resource type name is one of the reserved words, prepend `resource.`\n   - You only need to update the resource type part of the address\n   - Module and resource names themselves don't need changes\n5. **Run `terraform validate`** again to confirm the changes are correct\n\n#### Example Fixes\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (v1.9.0) - causes error in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.config\n  to   = local.app_config\n}\n\n# AFTER (v1.10.0) - now valid\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config\n  to   = resource.local.app_config\n}\n```\n\n```hcl\n# BEFORE (v1.9.0) - causes error in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = var.settings\n  to   = var.application_settings\n}\n\n# AFTER (v1.10.0) - now valid\nmoved {\n  from = data.var.settings\n  to   = data.var.application_settings\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n- \u274c Only updating the `from` address but forgetting to update the `to` address\n- \u274c Adding `resource.` to regular resource types that don't conflict with keywords\n- \u274c Misunderstanding that this only applies to the resource TYPE, not the resource NAME\n- \u274c Not running `terraform validate` to catch these issues early\n\n#### Verification\nRun `terraform validate` to ensure all `moved` blocks are correctly specified:\n```bash\nterraform validate\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. Sensitive Value Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\nTerraform v1.10 improves how sensitive marks are propagated through conditional expressions and `for` expressions. Marks are now combined from all values within the expression to ensure consistency in results and avoid losing sensitive information.\n\n**Key behavior change**: In v1.9, sensitive marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional expressions and unknown values. In v1.10, marks are preserved more accurately.\n\n#### Impact\n- **Improved accuracy**: Your configuration validation may now correctly identify more sensitive values\n- **Potential visibility changes**: You may see outputs marked as sensitive where they weren't in v1.9\n- **Breaking for some workflows**: If you relied on conditional expressions that \"hid\" sensitive marks, you'll see different behavior\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"include_password\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\n# In v1.9, this could lose the sensitive mark in certain conditions\nlocals {\n  config = var.include_password ? {\n    password = var.database_password\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  } : {\n    password = null\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  }\n}\n\n# Output could incorrectly show as non-sensitive\noutput \"config\" {\n  value     = local.config\n  sensitive = false  # This contradicts the actual sensitivity\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"include_password\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\n# In v1.10, the sensitive mark is properly preserved through the conditional\nlocals {\n  config = var.include_password ? {\n    password = var.database_password\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  } : {\n    password = null\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  }\n}\n\n# Output must now declare it as sensitive OR use nonsensitive() to explicitly remove marks\noutput \"config\" {\n  value = var.include_password ? local.config : {\n    password = null\n    user     = \"admin\"\n  }\n  sensitive = var.include_password  # Now correctly marks as sensitive when needed\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n1. **Run `terraform plan`** and check for warnings about sensitive values in outputs\n2. **Review outputs** that should have marked sensitive data:\n   - Add `sensitive = true` to the output declaration if the output may contain sensitive data\n   - OR use `nonsensitive()` function if you explicitly want to expose non-sensitive parts\n3. **Use the `nonsensitive()` function** to selectively remove sensitive marks:\n```hcl\n# This removes the sensitive mark while preserving non-sensitive parts\noutput \"non_sensitive_config\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(local.config.user)\n}\n```\n\n4. **For complex expressions**, ensure sensitive marks are handled explicitly:\n```hcl\n# When mixing sensitive and non-sensitive in conditionals\nlocals {\n  # Result will be sensitive if any branch uses sensitive data\n  value = var.use_secret ? var.secret_value : \"default_public_value\"\n}\n```\n\n5. **Run `terraform plan` again** to verify mark handling is correct\n\n#### Using `nonsensitive()` to Override Marks\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# You can remove the sensitive mark explicitly if needed\nlocals {\n  config = {\n    key = nonsensitive(var.api_key)  # Explicitly strip sensitive mark\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n- \u274c Not updating output blocks that now show warnings about missing `sensitive` declaration\n- \u274c Using `nonsensitive()` to hide sensitive values (they're still sensitive in state)\n- \u274c Assuming marks automatically propagate without declaring `sensitive = true` on outputs\n- \u274c Mixing sensitive and non-sensitive values without explicitly handling the result\n\n#### When Sensitive Marks Are Preserved\nMarks are combined from ALL values in a conditional expression:\n```hcl\n# Result is always sensitive (combines both branches)\nresult = condition ? sensitive_value : non_sensitive_value\n\n# Both branches have sensitive marks, so result is sensitive\nresult = condition ? sensitive_value_1 : sensitive_value_2\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\n#### What's New\nTerraform v1.10 introduces **ephemeral** data handling, which is available in public beta. Ephemeral values are available during Terraform operations but are NOT written to state files, plan files, or persisted between phases.\n\nThis is useful for managing temporary data like:\n- Authentication tokens with short expiration times\n- Temporary credentials generated during a Terraform run\n- Build artifacts that should not be stored\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n```hcl\n# Define an ephemeral input variable\nvariable \"temporary_auth_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"A short-lived authentication token that won't be stored in state\"\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # This local becomes implicitly ephemeral because it references an ephemeral variable\n  api_config = {\n    token = var.temporary_auth_token\n    endpoint = \"https://api.example.com\"\n  }\n}\n\nresource \"example_resource\" \"config\" {\n  # You can only use ephemeral values in specific contexts\n  token = var.temporary_auth_token\n}\n```\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs (Child Modules Only)\n```hcl\n# In a child module, you can create ephemeral outputs\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value     = var.temp_token\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary credentials not written to state\"\n}\n\n# This output can be referenced by parent modules but won't be persisted\n```\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull()` Function\nUse `ephemeralasnull()` to replace ephemeral values with `null` when you need non-ephemeral output:\n```hcl\nvariable \"secret_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Create a local that contains some ephemeral data\nlocals {\n  config = {\n    token = var.secret_token\n    name  = \"my-service\"\n  }\n}\n\n# Output the config with ephemeral values converted to null\noutput \"config\" {\n  value = ephemeralasnull(local.config)\n  description = \"Config with non-ephemeral values only\"\n  # Result: { token = null, name = \"my-service\" }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Considerations\n- Ephemeral values are in **public beta** and workflows may change\n- Ephemeral outputs are **only allowed in child modules**, not root modules\n- Ephemeral values can only be referenced in specific contexts:\n  - Other ephemeral variables\n  - Local values\n  - Ephemeral resources\n  - Ephemeral outputs\n- If you need to output ephemeral data, use `ephemeralasnull()` to make it non-ephemeral\n\n#### Using Ephemeral Values for Secrets\n```hcl\n# Replace sensitive + ephemeral workflow\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true  # NOT stored in state at all\n  # sensitive = true  # No longer needed when using ephemeral\n}\n\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"main\" {\n  password = var.db_password\n  # Password is temporary, exists only during the operation\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### S3 Backend: Native State Locking (Experimental)\n\n#### What's New\nThe S3 backend now supports optional S3 native state locking as an experimental feature. This allows you to use S3 Object Lock for state management without requiring DynamoDB.\n\n#### How It Works\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Enable S3 native locking (experimental)\n    use_lockfile   = true\n\n    # Can still use DynamoDB alongside S3 locking\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Lock File Naming\nWhen `use_lockfile = true`:\n- Lock file is placed in the same location as the state file\n- Named identically to the state file with `.tflock` extension\n- Example: if state is `prod/terraform.tfstate`, lock is `prod/terraform.tfstate.tflock`\n\n#### Important: IAM and Bucket Policies\n**You must update your S3 bucket policies and IAM policies** to include permissions for the lock file:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Principal\": {\n        \"AWS\": \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role\"\n      },\n      \"Action\": [\n        \"s3:GetObject\",\n        \"s3:PutObject\",\n        \"s3:DeleteObject\"\n      ],\n      \"Resource\": [\n        \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/*\",\n        \"arn:aws:s3:::my-terraform-state/*.tflock\"  # Add this line\n      ]\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\n1. **Update IAM permissions** to allow access to `.tflock` files\n2. **Enable `use_lockfile`** in your S3 backend configuration\n3. **DynamoDB locking** is still supported and will be used alongside S3 locking\n4. **Future versions** will deprecate DynamoDB-based locking\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Testing\n```bash\n# 1. Validate your current configuration with v1.9\nterraform validate\n\n# 2. Create a test plan\nterraform plan -out=test.tfplan\n\n# 3. Verify the plan makes sense\nterraform show test.tfplan\n```\n\n### Migration Testing\n```bash\n# 1. Upgrade Terraform\nterraform version  # Should show v1.10.0 or later\n\n# 2. Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# 3. Check for any issues\n# This should report any deprecated attribute usage\nterraform plan\n\n# 4. If using S3 backend with IAM role attributes:\n# - Update to assume_role block\n# - Run: terraform init\n# - Verify: terraform plan\n\n# 5. If using moved blocks with reserved keywords:\n# - Check validate output for errors\n# - Update address syntax\n# - Run: terraform validate\n```\n\n### Specific Test Cases\n\n#### Test S3 Backend Changes\n```bash\n# After updating assume_role block\ncd your-terraform-config/\nterraform init\n\n# Verify state is accessible\nterraform state list\n\n# Try a plan operation\nterraform plan\n```\n\n#### Test Moved Block Changes\n```bash\n# Run validation to catch syntax errors\nterraform validate\n\n# If there are moved blocks, check plan\nterraform plan\n# Should show successful moves, not errors\n```\n\n#### Test Sensitive Mark Changes\n```bash\n# Plan should show outputs with correct sensitive marking\nterraform plan\n\n# Check if any outputs should have sensitive = true\nterraform plan -json | grep -A5 \"sensitive\"\n```\n\n#### Test Ephemeral Values (if used)\n```bash\n# Ephemeral variables should work in plan\nterraform plan -var 'temp_token=short-lived-value'\n\n# Value should not appear in state\nterraform state show <resource>\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Rolling Back from v1.10 to v1.9\n\nIf you need to rollback to v1.9:\n\n#### S3 Backend Rollback\n```bash\n# 1. Convert assume_role block back to root-level attributes\n# OLD (v1.10) - in terraform { backend \"s3\" { } }\n# assume_role {\n#   role_arn           = \"arn:...\"\n#   session_name       = \"session\"\n#   external_id        = \"id\"\n# }\n\n# NEW (v1.9) - in terraform { backend \"s3\" { } }\n# role_arn                       = \"arn:...\"\n# session_name                   = \"session\"\n# external_id                    = \"id\"\n\n# 2. Reinitialize backend\nterraform init\n\n# 3. Verify state is accessible\nterraform plan\n```\n\n#### Moved Block Rollback\n```bash\n# 1. Remove \"resource.\" prefixes from moved block addresses\n# OLD (v1.10)\n# moved {\n#   from = resource.local.example\n#   to   = resource.local.renamed\n# }\n\n# NEW (v1.9)\n# moved {\n#   from = local.example\n#   to   = local.renamed\n# }\n\n# 2. Validate\nterraform validate\n```\n\n#### Downgrade Process\n```bash\n# 1. Make configuration changes as noted above\n# 2. Uninstall v1.10\nterraform version\n\n# 3. Install v1.9\n# Use your package manager or download from releases.hashicorp.com\n\n# 4. Verify\nterraform version  # Should show v1.9.x\n\n# 5. Test\nterraform validate\nterraform plan\n```\n\n### Safe Rollback Checklist\n- [ ] Configuration changes reverted\n- [ ] Terraform binary downgraded to v1.9\n- [ ] `terraform init` completed successfully\n- [ ] `terraform validate` passes\n- [ ] `terraform plan` completes without errors\n- [ ] Team members notified of rollback\n\n---\n\n## Common Issues and Solutions\n\n### Issue: \"keyword X is reserved and cannot be used\"\n**Cause**: Using a resource type name that matches a reserved keyword without the `resource.` prefix\n```hcl\n# \u274c Wrong\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = local.renamed\n}\n\n# \u2705 Correct\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = resource.local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n### Issue: S3 Backend refuses deprecated attributes\n**Cause**: Using old root-level IAM attributes instead of `assume_role` block\n```hcl\n# \u274c Won't work in v1.10\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    role_arn     = \"arn:...\"\n    session_name = \"session\"\n  }\n}\n\n# \u2705 Correct way\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn     = \"arn:...\"\n      session_name = \"session\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Issue: Output marked as sensitive unexpectedly\n**Cause**: v1.10 now correctly preserves sensitive marks through conditionals\n```hcl\n# Add sensitive = true to outputs that contain potentially sensitive data\noutput \"config\" {\n  value     = local.config\n  sensitive = var.include_password  # Set based on content\n}\n\n# OR use nonsensitive() to explicitly remove marks\noutput \"public_config\" {\n  value = {\n    user = nonsensitive(local.config.user)\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Issue: \"Ephemeral value not allowed here\"\n**Cause**: Trying to use ephemeral value in a non-ephemeral context\n```hcl\n# \u274c Wrong - using ephemeral variable in a regular resource\nvariable \"token\" {\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\noutput \"token\" {\n  value = var.token  # Error: can't persist ephemeral to state\n}\n\n# \u2705 Correct ways:\noutput \"token\" {\n  value     = var.token\n  ephemeral = true  # Mark output as ephemeral (child modules only)\n}\n\n# OR in root module, convert to non-ephemeral:\noutput \"config\" {\n  value = {\n    user = \"admin\"\n    # token omitted - not using ephemeral value\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Terraform v1.10 Release Notes](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [S3 Backend Configuration Reference](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Moved Block Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/moved)\n- [Ephemeral Variables Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables#exclude-values-from-state)\n- [Sensitive Data in State](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/state/sensitive-data)\n- [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)\n\n---\n\n## Support and Questions\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Check the error message carefully** - Terraform usually provides clear guidance on what needs to change\n2. **Run `terraform validate`** to catch syntax and configuration errors\n3. **Review the CHANGELOG** for detailed information on specific changes\n4. **Test in a non-production environment** first\n5. **Post in the [Terraform Community Forum](https://discuss.hashicorp.com/c/terraform-core)** if you encounter unexpected behavior\n\n---\n\n## Upgrade Summary Checklist\n\n- [ ] Review all S3 backend configurations for deprecated IAM attributes\n- [ ] Update S3 backend configurations to use `assume_role` block\n- [ ] Update IAM/bucket policies to allow lock file access (if using `use_lockfile`)\n- [ ] Review all `moved` blocks for reserved keyword resource type names\n- [ ] Update `moved` block syntax to use `resource.` prefix where needed\n- [ ] Run `terraform validate` on all configurations\n- [ ] Test `terraform plan` in a safe environment\n- [ ] Review output blocks for missing `sensitive` declarations\n- [ ] Test with `terraform apply` on a non-critical resource if possible\n- [ ] Document any configuration changes for your team\n- [ ] Update team documentation and runbooks\n\n",

# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide

## Overview

Terraform v1.10.0 (released November 27, 2024) is a minor release in the stable v1.0 series that introduces new features and fixes for issues in v1.9.0. This guide covers the breaking changes and behavioral updates that may require changes to your Terraform configurations.

### Major Themes
- **S3 Backend Improvements**: Removal of deprecated IAM role attributes and support for S3 native state locking
- **Moved Block Enhancements**: Better handling of resource type names that match reserved keywords
- **Sensitive Value Handling**: Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions
- **New Ephemeral Feature**: Support for ephemeral variables, outputs, and resources that aren't persisted to state

## Breaking Changes

### 1. S3 Backend: IAM Role Assumption Attribute Removal

#### What Changed
Terraform v1.10 removes deprecated root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend configuration. These attributes have been replaced with a structured `assume_role` block that provides better organization and clarity.

The following attributes have been **removed and are no longer supported**:
- `role_arn`
- `session_name`
- `external_id`
- `assume_role_duration_seconds`
- `assume_role_policy`
- `assume_role_policy_arns`
- `assume_role_tags`
- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`

#### Before (v1.9.0)
```hcl
terraform {
  backend "s3" {
    bucket     = "my-terraform-state"
    key        = "prod/terraform.tfstate"
    region     = "us-east-1"

    # Deprecated attributes - will NOT work in v1.10
    role_arn                       = "arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/terraform-role"
    session_name                   = "terraform-session"
    external_id                    = "my-external-id"
    assume_role_durati
... (truncated)
